- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Bounded but Potentially Resource-Intensive Pagination Loop
  > The fetch_all() helper in references/parameters.md implements a pagination loop with configurable max_pages (default 50) and max_records (default 500,000) limits. While bounded, requesting up to 500,000 records with page sizes of 10,000 could result in significant memory consumption and prolonged execution. The loop also includes a 0.1-second sleep between pages, which is minimal rate limiting. The retry logic for HTTP 429 uses exponential backoff up to 3 attempts, which is reasonable.
  > File: `references/parameters.md`
  > **Remediation:** Consider reducing default max_records to a more conservative value (e.g., 50,000) and increasing the sleep interval between pages to at least 0.5 seconds to reduce resource pressure and be a better API citizen.

### xlsx — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Referenced File 'openpyxl.py' Not Found in Skill Package
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference a file named 'openpyxl.py' which was not found in the skill package. This missing file reference could indicate an incomplete package or a documentation error. If the agent attempts to read this file, it may fail or fall back to unexpected behavior. This is a minor documentation/packaging issue with no direct security impact.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure all referenced files are included in the skill package. If 'openpyxl.py' is not needed, remove the reference from SKILL.md. If it is needed, add the file to the package.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Dependencies in Installation Instructions
  > The SKILL.md installation instructions use 'uv pip install openpyxl pandas' and 'uv pip install python-calamine' and 'uv pip install defusedxml' without version pins. This means the skill will install whatever the latest version of these packages is at install time, which could include compromised or breaking versions. Supply chain attacks against popular packages like pandas or openpyxl could affect users of this skill.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin all dependencies to specific versions, e.g., 'uv pip install openpyxl==3.1.5 pandas==2.2.2 defusedxml==0.7.1'. Consider providing a requirements.txt or pyproject.toml with pinned versions and hash verification.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Dynamic C Code Compilation and LD_PRELOAD Injection via gcc
  > The soffice.py script compiles a C shim at runtime using gcc and injects it via LD_PRELOAD into LibreOffice subprocesses. While the C source is hardcoded within the Python file (not fetched from external sources), this pattern is inherently risky: it compiles and loads native code at runtime, modifies the dynamic linker environment, and intercepts low-level socket system calls. The shim is stored in a user-owned cache directory (~/.cache/xlsx-skill/lo-shim/) with hash verification. If an attacker could modify the _SHIM_SOURCE string or the cache directory contents, they could achieve arbitrary code execution. The hash verification uses SHA-256 of the source string itself (not a hardcoded expected hash), so it only detects cache corruption, not source tampering.
  > File: `scripts/office/soffice.py`
  > **Remediation:** This is a legitimate workaround for sandboxed environments. Consider documenting this behavior prominently in the skill description so users are aware that gcc may be invoked and native code compiled. The hash verification could be strengthened by comparing against a hardcoded expected hash rather than a self-referential hash of the source. Ensure the cache directory permissions (0o700) are enforced before writing.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access in LibreOffice Subprocess Environment
  > The soffice.py helper constructs a minimal environment for LibreOffice subprocesses by selectively copying specific keys from os.environ (PATH, HOME, LANG, LC_ALL, LC_CTYPE, TMPDIR, TMP, TEMP, USER). While this is intentionally restrictive and designed to avoid leaking secrets, the static analyzer flagged it as a potential env var exfiltration pattern. In context, this is a legitimate security measure — the code explicitly avoids copying the full environment. However, the selected keys (HOME, USER, TMPDIR) do expose some user identity information to the LibreOffice subprocess. No network calls are made with this data; it is passed only to a local soffice process. This is LOW severity as the behavior is intentional and appropriate for the stated purpose.
  > File: `scripts/office/soffice.py`
  > **Remediation:** This pattern is intentional and appropriate. No remediation needed. The comment in the code correctly documents the intent. Consider adding a note that HOME and USER are required by LibreOffice for profile directory resolution.
